    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1847641370" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1847641370" />
    <a title="emi" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/34410191-emi"><img alt="emi" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603747413p2/34410191.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1847641370?book_show_action=true">Dec 23, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="emi" class="user" itemprop="url" name="emi" href="/user/show/34410191-emi">emi</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/34410191-emi?shelf=2017">2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/34410191-emi?shelf=2-stars">2-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/34410191-emi?shelf=girl-meets-boy-contemporaries">girl-meets-boy-contemporaries</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/34410191-emi?shelf=forgettable">forgettable</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/34410191-emi?shelf=i-spent-my-money-on-this">i-spent-my-money-on-this</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1847641370" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11543236546483850505"><i>2.75/5 stars</i><br/><br/><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>I don’t entirely understand how anyone gets a boyfriend. Or a girlfriend. It just seems like the most impossible odds. You have to have a crush on the exact right person at the exact right moment. And they have to like you back. A perfect alignment of feelings and circumstances. It’s almost unfathomable that it happens as often as it does.</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br/>I think there should be a law in place that bans terrible books, especially when they are a follow up to an incredible debut. <i>
  <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/19547856.Simon_vs__the_Homo_Sapiens_Agenda' title='Simon vs. the Homo Sapiens Agenda by Becky Albertalli' rel='nofollow noopener'>Simon </a></i></span>
  <span id="freeText11543236546483850505" style="display:none"><i>2.75/5 stars</i><br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>I don’t entirely understand how anyone gets a boyfriend. Or a girlfriend. It just seems like the most impossible odds. You have to have a crush on the exact right person at the exact right moment. And they have to like you back. A perfect alignment of feelings and circumstances. It’s almost unfathomable that it happens as often as it does.</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br />I think there should be a law in place that bans terrible books, especially when they are a follow up to an incredible debut. <i>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/19547856.Simon_vs__the_Homo_Sapiens_Agenda" title="Simon vs. the Homo Sapiens Agenda by Becky Albertalli" rel="nofollow noopener">Simon vs. the Homo Sapiens Agenda</a>
</i> was such a well-executed novel that I reasonably assumed this one would be too. Turns out, everything I knew about the universe was wrong because this book is absolutely nothing like <i>Simon.</i><br /><br /><i>The Upside of Unrequited?</i> More like the <i>The Downside of Disappointment</i> amiright?<br /><br />Unpopular opinion time! As this review has a 4.08 average rating and soooo many of my friends on here seem to love it. I just wasn't one of them. <br /><br />The worst part about this book is that it had so much potential to address different social issues but instead it decided to throw itself in the chasm of stupidity. Literally, all I got out of this book was that the only way to be confident with yourself is to have a boyfriend. Exactly the kind of message I want teenagers to be reading. <br /><br />We were also told the main character has anxiety, which I was excited about. It is important to have representation of mental illness in books. Except, we were only ever told the main character has anxiety. I might be wrong, and if I am please correct me, but I don't remember a scene where anxiety played a major role. Not really the representation I was hoping for, but I guess it's still there and that should count for something. <br /><br />Now, usually, this is when I would try to summarize the plot of a book in a paragraph or a small essay or anything, but there isn't even enough plot in this book to do that. There isn't any plot in this book. The entire thing is just a girl, who complains about not having a boyfriend, trying to find a boyfriend. Which shouldn't be hard, honestly, as there are not one, but two possible love interests in this book. That's right folks, packaged inside this blue tree corpse is a love triangle. And not even an "I hate love triangles and rather not read about one, but I guess this one is salvageable" love triangle. It is one of the weakest freaking frack love triangles I have ever seen. It was Complaining Girl vs Boy She Has Nothing In Common With vs Boy She Has Slightly More In Common With But Also Not Really. I couldn't' even pretend to muster up enough energy to root for somebody. <br /><br />Then the boy who Molly eventually ends up with, I wasn't too sold on their relationship. I didn't feel like they had that funny banter and great chemistry I crave in a YA contemporary novel. It was more like I could see them dating for a few weeks or months then moving on with their life. They didn't have enough in common or enough deep conversations for me to buy the fact that they might spend the rest of their lives together. But, again, that just might be me. <br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b> "I'm on the toilet at the 9:30 Club, and I'm wondering how mermaids pee." </b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br />Let's talk about the writing real quick, shall we? The first chapter or two tricked me. I thought the writing was gonna be great. In fact, the first line of this book might be my favorite first line in all the books I've ever read. An entire star was given just for it. But, unfortunately, that was the best sentence in the entire book. The way everything is worded is like Molly is speaking her story aloud and someone is trying to transcribe it. Or maybe like how I write my reviews, as if I'm speaking a reader, in this case you, directly. Sometimes the writing was like this. Other times IT WAS LIKE THIS. It was cool for a little while, but by chapter three I was beyond annoyed. For a review or a blog post or anything, this way of writing is cool. It's only a thousand words or so of it. Enough to read it and move on with your life. But when it's 350 pages of it, you can imagine the agony. <br /><br />Molly the MC would be talking about one thing, going into detail about it and everything, and then by the next paragraph she'd have gotten distracted and would be talking about something else. And when she texted someone, which was all the freaking time, she would describe every single emoji used in detail. And there were a lot of emojis. Do you know the cringing emoji? Insert him here. <br /><br />I think now is the perfect time to talk characters?<br /><br /><b>Molly.</b> All she did was complain. And complain some more. And never stood up for herself. She'd get insanely jealous if someone else was even remotely interested in the same guy. There was no character development other than she started off forever along and ended up with a boyfriend. Next. <br /><br /><b>Cassie.</b> She was a bitch the entire book but that was dismissed because she's the main character's twin sister. She'd drag Molly everywhere if she wanted to go or not, treat her like crap, stop talking to her for no good reason, and so on. But she's just a sister who is in love so that's okay.<br /><br /><b>Reid.</b> I have neutral feelings for Reid. I didn't feel like there were enough scenes of him to really form an opinion. <br /><br /><b>Will.</b> What even was the point of him? We could have taken him out and had the exact same story. 0/5 stars for Will. <br /><br /><b>Olivia and Abby.</b> I know one of them lives over in Georiga with Simon, but I got these two confused so many times in the entire book. They were pretty interchangeable, however, so I guess that was okay. <br /><br /><b>Patty and Nadine.</b> There were times when I was like, "Wow, they are such realistic parents" and then there were times when I was like, "What moms would allow their two daughters to have a sleepover with so many people of different sexes?" I wish their characters were more consistent, tbh. <br /><br />This book wasn't horrible though. I even considered giving it three stars just because there were parts that I did love. When Simon showed up in two different scene, that was my favorite parts. I love Simon. Then also the last chapter was the cutest, sweetest thing. And the abundance of diversity was amazing. There was representation of so many different sexualities and races and body types. It wouldn't be hard to find somebody in this book you can relate to. <br /><br />But in the end, this book just isn't for me.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11543236546483850505" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1774688282" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1774688282" />
    <a title="Kai" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/41788524-kai"><img alt="Kai" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1573562141p2/41788524.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1774688282?book_show_action=true">Oct 03, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kai" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kai" href="/user/show/41788524-kai">Kai</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41788524-kai?shelf=2018">2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41788524-kai?shelf=queer">queer</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1774688282" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1872370549281681681"><i>“I want to know what it feels like to have crushes that could conceivably maybe one day turn into boyfriends.”</i><br/><br/>This was once again a very honest and real story by Becky Albertalli. The reason why books like Becky's resonate so much with teenagers and young adults is because in them we feel understood. We are represented. Our feelings and thoughts are valid. We see ourselves in these characters, in their struggles and in their dreams.<br/><br/>I also love that Becky talks this openly about sex. And not just</span>
  <span id="freeText1872370549281681681" style="display:none"><i>“I want to know what it feels like to have crushes that could conceivably maybe one day turn into boyfriends.”</i><br /><br />This was once again a very honest and real story by Becky Albertalli. The reason why books like Becky's resonate so much with teenagers and young adults is because in them we feel understood. We are represented. Our feelings and thoughts are valid. We see ourselves in these characters, in their struggles and in their dreams.<br /><br />I also love that Becky talks this openly about sex. And not just straight sex. It reminds me of Patrick Ness' novel <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/31194576.Release" title="Release by Patrick Ness" rel="nofollow noopener">Release</a>. And yet again, both authors, Ness as well as Allbertalli, could've gone a bit further. Most of the time these open talks about sex and sexuality stopped in the middle of the conversation, with so many questions still unaswered. Then again, these are YA novels, not sex ed books...but still.<br /><br />All that is left to say is that I seriously cannot wait for <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/31180248.Leah_on_the_Offbeat" title="Leah on the Offbeat by Becky Albertalli" rel="nofollow noopener">Leah on the Offbeat</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/36260157.What_If_It_s_Us" title="What If It's Us by Becky Albertalli" rel="nofollow noopener">What If It's Us</a>. I want them NOW.<br /><br /><a href="https://www.instagram.com/fantasticbooksandwheretofindem/" rel="nofollow noopener">Find more of my books on Instagram</a></span>

          </span>

<div id="review_2004574198" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2004574198" />
    <a title="Always Pouting" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/48650982-always-pouting"><img alt="Always Pouting" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1483476563p2/48650982.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2004574198?book_show_action=true">Jun 16, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Always Pouting" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Always Pouting" href="/user/show/48650982-always-pouting">Always Pouting</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2004574198" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9329830734924509266">During a night out with her twin Cassie, Molly meets a girl in the bathroom who she instantly knows is Cassie's dream girl. The girl from the bathroom, Mina, and Cassie hit it off and Cassie manages to get Mina's number that night. Molly is happy for her sister but at the same time Cassie's new relationship begins to make her think about her own lack of a love life and the growing distance between her and Cassie. Molly is used to being the closest person to Cassie and has a hard time learning to</span>
  <span id="freeText9329830734924509266" style="display:none">During a night out with her twin Cassie, Molly meets a girl in the bathroom who she instantly knows is Cassie's dream girl. The girl from the bathroom, Mina, and Cassie hit it off and Cassie manages to get Mina's number that night. Molly is happy for her sister but at the same time Cassie's new relationship begins to make her think about her own lack of a love life and the growing distance between her and Cassie. Molly is used to being the closest person to Cassie and has a hard time learning to deal with Cassie having someone else she goes to. Molly also hasn't ever felt as attractive as Cassie, mostly due to her weight. Molly is always told to try to put herself out there and do more but none of her friends understand that she has to work harder to protect herself from getting hurt. Even though she's like 27 guys Molly hasn't done anything with a boy and she can't help but question how much of it has to do with her as a person and people's inability to want her. <br /><br />So when Cassie tries to push Molly together with Mina's best guy friend, Molly might even be open to it. Too bad her coworker Reid is the one she can't seem to stop thinking about. Reid is comfortable and dorky and right off the bat Molly felt comfortable around him. She just doesn't know how to be sure about his feelings for her. There's also the fact that this will only make her and Cassie's relationship change even more. <br /><br />I really liked this book, it was really adorable. Molly does a lot of things that I personally wouldn't do or say but I didn't feel like that kept me from connecting with her or the book. I've also been there, where you like people but you won't let yourself even hope that someone could ever like you back. Its really relateable especially wanting someone to want you because everyone else seems to have people who want them so how come no one wants you. I really thought Cassie was being god damn annoying though. She doesn't have to be up Molly's ass but she definitely could've been much kinder to her and actually have tried to listen to what Molly wanted. <br /><br />Anyway I enjoyed this book a lot even though I don't think I'm in the place where I need something like this but I do think it be even better for someone who is in that place that Molly's in and dealing with growing up and learning to be in relationships and readjusting to friendships changing. Also it was pretty good with the diversity and I know that's important to people.<br /><br />Also on a totally separate note how do girls just like find other girls who like girls like I truly dont get how anyone does it. It's so much easier with boys because they're so obvious and kind of just make sure you know they're interested. Confusing man confusing.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9329830734924509266" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1991451194" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1991451194" />
    <a title="Whitney Atkinson" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14457130-whitney-atkinson"><img alt="Whitney Atkinson" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1550868411p2/14457130.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1991451194?book_show_action=true">Oct 25, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Whitney Atkinson" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Whitney Atkinson" href="/user/show/14457130-whitney-atkinson">Whitney Atkinson</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14457130-whitney-atkinson?shelf=lgbtqiap">lgbtqiap</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14457130-whitney-atkinson?shelf=read-in-2017">read-in-2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14457130-whitney-atkinson?shelf=unhauled">unhauled</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14457130-whitney-atkinson?shelf=mental-health">mental-health</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1991451194" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1038727027855782242">This started out so promising, but it just wasn't for me. i thought i would be able to relate to it because fat mc with anxiety, but our personalities and insecurities were completely different and i found i actually really didn't see myself in molly at all. the biggest problem, i think, is that this is a book i wish i'd read 5-6 years ago. now, i'm beyond the part of my life where i'm self-conscious and awkward, so it did nothing for me to read about that.<br/><br/>i wasn’t a fan of the repetition of “i’</span>
  <span id="freeText1038727027855782242" style="display:none">This started out so promising, but it just wasn't for me. i thought i would be able to relate to it because fat mc with anxiety, but our personalities and insecurities were completely different and i found i actually really didn't see myself in molly at all. the biggest problem, i think, is that this is a book i wish i'd read 5-6 years ago. now, i'm beyond the part of my life where i'm self-conscious and awkward, so it did nothing for me to read about that.<br /><br />i wasn’t a fan of the repetition of “i’m so embarrassed about my body” and the “i blush every time i look at a boy.” if this had only been brought up a few times then it would have been more bearable, but every single scene was just contingent on those 2 pieces of inner monologue, and it got old. i think a younger whitney would have appreciated this. i’m out of the stage where im ashamed of my clothing size and dont want people judging me, but i could see how a younger me would be more like molly. by the end of the book this just seemed like one of those “i got a boyfriend and now i love myself!” stories. as a fat girl, the message to me just kinda seemed like “i can’t accept myself until i know i’m lovable." i would have loved to read a book about a fat girl coming to terms with her size, but this just felt very contingent on the love interest.<br /><br />additionally, this book is sort of about how molly has had 26 crushes that she never pursued and so she felt like she NEEDED to have a first kiss and get a boyfriend. 1) this is a little concerning to me, even though at the very end (sigh) one of her moms explains why she shouldn't worry about that, and 2) when everyone finds out molly has a boyfriend, the reaction of literally everyone was "wwHHAHHAAAATTTTTT???" which i thought was a little disturbing. like, was there something about her that you thought would hinder her from getting a boyfriend? idk. it just seemed.... weird. it didn't read like it was trying to be funny or quirky.<br /><br />also, i'm just really not a fan of becky's writing style. a lot of the dialogue tended to be cheesy and unrealistic. it was quick to read, just not…. idk. i couldn’t see myself in any of the conversations. even the adults in this book talk like they’re 12. by the end of the book i was reading some of the text messages and dialogue out loud to bonnie and we were both like ... that's weird. also no one would ever talk like that. also i'm cringing.<br /><br />and molly's anxiety just kinda got swept under the rug? it mentions she takes zoloft, but this book never actually discusses panic attacks or dealing with feelings of anxiety, other than feelings of self-consciousness (mentioned earlier). I guess i was expecting more on this front, and it just didn't deliver.<br /><br />i just had really high expectations for this book, and it ended up not being as relatable as i thought it would be. if you'd given this to me while i was in middle school, though, i'm sure i would have loved it, so i'm trying not to be too critical on it because i know molly's story will still be uplifting for a lot of young readers.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1038727027855782242" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1348457785" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1348457785" />
    <a title="Natalie Monroe" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6688207-natalie-monroe"><img alt="Natalie Monroe" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1339730817p2/6688207.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1348457785?book_show_action=true">Jan 04, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Natalie Monroe" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Natalie Monroe" href="/user/show/6688207-natalie-monroe">Natalie Monroe</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=sugar-spice-n-everything-nice">sugar-spice-n-everything-nice</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=love-wins">love-wins</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=my-inner-feminist-cries-with-joy">my-inner-feminist-cries-with-joy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1348457785" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7840030834211415413"><b>4.5 stars</b><br/><br/><blockquote>
  <i>"If I like a guy, I'm supposed to tell him. Maybe in Cassie's world, you can do that and have it end in making out. But I'm not so sure it works that way for fat girls."</i>
</blockquote><br/><br/>So this review is going to be a little personal. By that, I mean I'm going to ramble and waste ten minutes of your time, depending on how fast you read. Free feel to grab a bagel.<br/><br/>When I was sixteen, the standard YA age, I was a <b>painfully introverted kid.</b> Not the fun John Green kind, but the really sad kind that makes</span>
  <span id="freeText7840030834211415413" style="display:none"><b>4.5 stars</b><br><br><blockquote>
  <i>"If I like a guy, I'm supposed to tell him. Maybe in Cassie's world, you can do that and have it end in making out. But I'm not so sure it works that way for fat girls."</i>
</blockquote><br><br>So this review is going to be a little personal. By that, I mean I'm going to ramble and waste ten minutes of your time, depending on how fast you read. Free feel to grab a bagel.<br><br>When I was sixteen, the standard YA age, I was a <b>painfully introverted kid.</b> Not the fun John Green kind, but the really sad kind that makes you feel awkward when they sit next your table in the cafeteria. Part of it was me, part of it was my physical disability—it wasn't convenient for me to go to places. I didn't have any close friends, except for the occasional classmate you'd say hi to during Biology.<br><br>I was also achingly, morbidly <i>desperate</i> for a boyfriend. I had loads of crushes, but never acted on them. Because, you see, I also had <b>massive insecurity issues.</b> (Sixteen-year-old Natalie sounds like a mess, doesn't she?) My disability is a form of muscular dystrophy. Right now, I use a wheelchair, but back then I still walked with the help of a cane. My atrophied muscles affected my posture and movements, so I walked like a cartoon duck, all awkward angles and wheezing breaths. <br><br>I was dying on the vine for romance, but secretly believed I would never find it because, well, look at that mirror. Look at who you are.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1483609345ra/21629804.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>A huge part of why I enjoyed The Upside of Unrequited so much is <b>I <i>am</i> Molly.</b> Or I was her. I identified with her so much, and I don't even care if there's a tiny slice of wish-fulfillment going on—I cheered like a Cubs fan when Molly got her first kiss. It was magical and sweet and nostalgic. In that moment, I was sixteen again, with the wisdom of twenties Natalie to balance it out.<br><br>Molly speaks to us. The invisible girls with thirsty hearts (Shamelessly stealing from <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7514925.Tiger_Lily" title="Tiger Lily by Jodi Lynn Anderson" rel="nofollow noopener">Tiger Lily</a>). Maybe it's pathetic. But we all feel insecure about our bodies at some point in time, one way or another. You don't have to be fat to identify with The Upside of Unrequited's message of beauty and self-acceptance. It goes far beyond a boy loving you, which is why I mentioned Molly's shoes are tempered with twenties Natalie's mentality.<br><br><b>Look at that mirror, girl. You're fucking beautiful.</b><br><br>Other things I want to mention is the <b>amazing diversity.</b> There are characters of all races and genders. White characters are pointed out because it's foolish to presume white is the norm. Relationships between female characters are <b>as big of a part in the narrative</b> as the romance, and the plot thread with Molly and Olivia is simply magnificent. <br><br>And this: <br><br><blockquote>
  <i>"Because I don't want to be a girl who needs a boyfriend,"I say.<br><br>"Well, of course you don't need one,"Nadine says. "But it's okay to want one."</i>
</blockquote><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1483609345ra/21629805.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Every bit as good as <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/19547856.Simon_vs__the_Homo_Sapiens_Agenda" title="Simon vs. the Homo Sapiens Agenda by Becky Albertalli" rel="nofollow noopener">Simon vs. the Homo Sapiens Agenda</a>. I would wager even better.<br><br>(P.S. Sixteen-year-old Natalie turned out just fine. After all, she's here talking to you. ;) )</span>
  <a data-text-id="7840030834211415413" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2347456693" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2347456693" />
    <a title="Kaylin (The Re-Read Queen)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/47627265-kaylin-the-re-read-queen"><img alt="Kaylin (The Re-Read Queen)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1560356189p2/47627265.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2347456693?book_show_action=true">Aug 02, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kaylin (The Re-Read Queen)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kaylin (The Re-Read Queen)" href="/user/show/47627265-kaylin-the-re-read-queen">Kaylin (The Re-Read Queen)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47627265-kaylin-the-re-read-queen?shelf=lgbt">lgbt</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47627265-kaylin-the-re-read-queen?shelf=contemporaries">contemporaries</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47627265-kaylin-the-re-read-queen?shelf=almost-great">almost-great</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47627265-kaylin-the-re-read-queen?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2347456693" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3038437840796084605"><b>3 Stars</b> <br/><br/><i>
  <blockquote>”I mean, here’s the thing I don’t get. How do people come to expect that their crushes will be reciprocated? Like, how does that get to be your default assumption?”</blockquote>
</i> <br/><br/>I’ve officially three-starred every Becky Albertalli book and no one is more disappointed than me. Because here’s the thing— <b>Albertalli really and truly understands <i>being</i> a teenager.</b> She <i>gets</i> the dark/silly humor. She <i>gets</i> texting conversations. She <i>gets</i> the awkwardness and she <i>gets</i> the uncertainty and anxiety that can co</span>
  <span id="freeText3038437840796084605" style="display:none"><b>3 Stars</b> <br /><br /><i>
  <blockquote>”I mean, here’s the thing I don’t get. How do people come to expect that their crushes will be reciprocated? Like, how does that get to be your default assumption?”</blockquote>
</i> <br /><br />I’ve officially three-starred every Becky Albertalli book and no one is more disappointed than me. Because here’s the thing— <b>Albertalli really and truly understands <i>being</i> a teenager.</b> She <i>gets</i> the dark/silly humor. She <i>gets</i> texting conversations. She <i>gets</i> the awkwardness and she <i>gets</i> the uncertainty and anxiety that can come with trying to decide who you are and what you want. <br /><br />Molly is an exceptionally relatable narrator to me, and shows Albertalli also understands what being a plus-sized teenager can be like. While Molly’s friends and twin sister have flourishing love lives, she only seems to crush from afar. The way Molly relates her perception of self (and the notable ways she <i>doesn’t</i>) to her continued single-status open <b> some really important discussions about society’s expectations and how it can warp our own.</b> Molly is comfortable in her own skin, but she also never assumes her crushes could like her back.<br /><br />There’s one point after Molly’s sister (Cassie) starts dating her girlfriend <b>(yes there’s also awesome lesbian and Pan rep!)</b> when Cassie’s dating advice is just “tell them you like them” and Molly is <i>flabbergasted.</i> She doesn’t comprehend how that could not be embarrassing. This hit me <i>hard</i> and spoke so honestly about so much of my high-school experience I wish I could rate this higher. <br /><br />But unfortunately, <b>Molly continues to define herself through her relationship status.</b> At first it just seems part of her character arc— her determination to <i>finally</i> be kissed, <i>finally</i> be in a relationship and <i>finally</i> feel wanted are the driving force of the whole book. I hoped she’d realize how her identity was tied solely to what others (especially boys) think of her. I was thinking this single-minded intensity was purposeful... and... kinda? But <b>instead of developing her own sense of identity Molly gets that big-first kiss and suddenly feels validated.</b> <br /><br />So in a way, all the agency Molly acquires in the end feels bittersweet. <b>Because it almost feels like confirming her earlier assumptions— that getting a boyfriend <i>did</i> validate her.</b> Because until a man considered her attractive, what <i>right</i> did she have being confident???<br /><br /><b> Overall:</b> <br />All the stars for the honest, realistic portrayal of adolescence and the representation this offers. <br /><br />No stars for the harmful defining-myself-through-men mentality.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3038437840796084605" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2169502662" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2169502662" />
    <a title="Matthew" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16254355-matthew"><img alt="Matthew" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1464987365p2/16254355.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2169502662?book_show_action=true">Oct 17, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Matthew" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Matthew" href="/user/show/16254355-matthew">Matthew</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audiobook 9780062417886" href="/book/show/31143934-the-upside-of-unrequited">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">YA Fans</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16254355-matthew?shelf=2018">2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16254355-matthew?shelf=audio">audio</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16254355-matthew?shelf=coming-of-age">coming-of-age</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16254355-matthew?shelf=library">library</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16254355-matthew?shelf=gr_awards_2017">gr_awards_2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16254355-matthew?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2169502662" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4447121162600090731">This book was cute - it was exactly what I expect from YA and that is perfect!<br/><br/>While there is some LGBT theme in it like the authors last book, it is more of an accompanying theme, not the theme that drives the story. This book is more about body image and confidence. Our heroine, Molly, deals with being an overweight teenager and self-sabotaging herself because she is always assuming the worst. Also, because of her insecurities there is a lot of storyline based around how someone in her shoes vi</span>
  <span id="freeText4447121162600090731" style="display:none">This book was cute - it was exactly what I expect from YA and that is perfect!<br /><br />While there is some LGBT theme in it like the authors last book, it is more of an accompanying theme, not the theme that drives the story. This book is more about body image and confidence. Our heroine, Molly, deals with being an overweight teenager and self-sabotaging herself because she is always assuming the worst. Also, because of her insecurities there is a lot of storyline based around how someone in her shoes views relationships. All very interesting and well written.<br /><br />My favorite YA trope makes an appearance: lists. Seems like YA characters are always making lists. Molly doesn't let us down as she gives us a list of her crushes.<br /><br />Speaking of YA tropes - YA books always seem to make teens sound more sophisticated than I remember being and more sophisticated than I feel now (I'm looking at you, John Green!). With this book I think the author did a good job of making the teenagers seem more realistic in their dialogue.<br /><br />If you are a YA fan, this has to be on your list. If you enjoyed Simon, you won't be disappointed.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4447121162600090731" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2080565708" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2080565708" />
    <a title="Katie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7161764-katie"><img alt="Katie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1555967180p2/7161764.jpg" /></a>

<div id="review_1987683892" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1987683892" />
    <a title="Maureen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10762033-maureen"><img alt="Maureen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1398557569p2/10762033.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1987683892?book_show_action=true">May 02, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maureen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maureen" href="/user/show/10762033-maureen">Maureen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1987683892" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4086669491557156701">I'm crying because that ending was so beautiful????<br/><br/>Alright this book. I went in with really really high expectations and expecting that it would be a book of my HEART and I would relate a lot to the main character because of similar situations. And I did relate! Just not a lot. Or as much as I had hoped. Probably some of my disappointment (very minor disappointment!) comes from setting too high of expectations. BUT ON WITH THINGS I LOVED.<br/><br/>The diversity in this book was A+++++++ to infinity. It wa</span>
  <span id="freeText4086669491557156701" style="display:none">I'm crying because that ending was so beautiful????<br /><br />Alright this book. I went in with really really high expectations and expecting that it would be a book of my HEART and I would relate a lot to the main character because of similar situations. And I did relate! Just not a lot. Or as much as I had hoped. Probably some of my disappointment (very minor disappointment!) comes from setting too high of expectations. BUT ON WITH THINGS I LOVED.<br /><br />The diversity in this book was A+++++++ to infinity. It was so natural and wonderful and made sense in the story and there were so MANY THINGS. The main character has anxiety and talks about it openly, has two moms, her sister is a lesbian, her sister's love interest is Korean-American and pansexual, and that's just naming a *few* characters. It was JAM PACKED with well developed, diverse, authentic characters. I also loved how all of the characters, especially the family, were so supportive and great??? All the drama happened with change and things Molly was going through, not people being awful.<br /><br />I really did relate to Molly and her situation, though I've always been on the side of not really needing a boyfriend, I've been very selective about my crushes and basically never letting on that I liked anyone ever. SO RELATABLE. I also struggle with overthinking, though not to the extent that Molly does, which is probably partially from her anxiety that I don't personally struggle with.<br /><br />A small thing I loved learning about was Jewish culture and things I definitely didn't know about before. It was really fun learning about it!<br /><br />Things I didn't really love - the writing. I liked parts of it, but sometimes it felt too straightforward for me and I would've liked a little more flow and flower to it. I also didn't really love how much everyone needed to talk about sex? But that's always definitely a me thing and is probably something other people talk about and discuss a lot? But not me and not my friends. So it got to be a little much with that at times. <br /><br />Overall, really really liked it, not quite love level, but I really liked it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4086669491557156701" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('Ng8jVWGE4JNr6lEIQIlbcXv08bIa1rn9DeJeE6y8wYYMKUqH2top+8zB5Wm3fFGurasWetRbN5pWnBiiYf8zHA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('jQQ1v4xAYgLKdoW5lAkQmk8Udk5dNXV5iNQusmLm7WW3IlxtNx6ram1dMdhj/BpFmUuRhpO4+x7TqmgDr6Uf/w==')})
  }

<span id="freeTextContainer12590998874927219912">Becky Albertalli is the author of the acclaimed novels Simon vs. the Homo Sapiens Agenda (film: Love, Simon), The Upside of Unrequited, and Leah on the Offbeat. She is also the co-author of What If It's Us with Adam Silvera. A former clinical psychologist who specialized in working with children and teens, Becky lives with her family in Atlanta. You can visit her online at <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://www.beckyalbertalli.com'>www.beckyalbertalli.com</a>.</span>
